## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population P and time t, which is the right-hand side of a population dynamics ODE. Classical models involve density-dependent growth, carrying capacity effects, and potentially time-varying parameters.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate proportional to log of remaining capacity)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (strong Allee effect with minimum viable population)
- Von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic minus catabolic growth)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * (1 + c3) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent with hyperbolic saturation)
- Seasonal logistic: dP_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P * (1 - c3 * P) (logistic with periodic environmental forcing)
- Time-dependent exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth rate changing exponentially with time)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power growth dynamics)
- Delayed density effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * t * P (logistic with trend in environment)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- dP/dt proportional to P → exponential/Malthusian growth regime; look for linear term in P
- dP/dt with P*(1 - P/K) structure → logistic density dependence producing a parabolic nullcline in P
- Negative quadratic term in P (P²) → carrying capacity / self-limitation at high density
- Cubic terms in P (P³ or P*(P-a)*(K-P)) → Allee effect or bistability with critical population thresholds
- Logarithmic dependence log(K/P) → Gompertz-type growth with asymmetric approach to carrying capacity
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) multiplying growth terms → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing
- Ratio P/(1+cP) → saturating per-capita reproduction rate (contest competition)
- Growth rate that changes sign at specific P values → equilibrium points; number of sign changes indicates number of stable/unstable equilibria
- Time appearing only through periodic functions → environmental seasonality without secular trend
- Difference of power laws (P^a - P^b) → metabolic scaling or competing anabolic/catabolic processes

This gives: `c0*P² + c1*P + c2*P/(c3*P + 1) + c5*P^c4`

But the GT has `P²/(c*P+1)`, not `P/(c*P+1)`. These are different rational functions. `P/(c3*P+1)` vs `P²/(c*P+1)` — can't match.

**Candidate 12:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2/(P*c3 + 1)`

= `c0*P² + c1*P + c2*P/(c3*P + 1)`. The rational term is `c2*P/(c3*P+1)`, but GT needs `P²/(c*P+1)`. Not equivalent.

**Candidate 15:** `P²*c0 + P*c1/(P + c2) + P*c3`

= `c0*P² + c1*P/(P+c2) + c3*P`. The rational part is `P/(P+c2)` not `P²/(P+c2)`. Not matching.

**Candidate 5:** `P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2/(P + c3) + P*c4`

= `c0*P³ + c1*P² + c2*P/(P+c3) + c4*P`. Setting c0=0: `c1*P² + c2*P/(P+c3) + c4*P`. Still `P/(P+c3)` not `P²/(...)`.

**Candidate 6:** `P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P²*c2 + P*c3/(P + c4) + P*c5`

Setting c0=0: `(c1+c2)*P² + c3*P/(P+c4) + c5*P`. Same issue.

**Candidate 16:** `P³*c0/(P+c1) + P²*c2/(P+c1) + P*c3/(P+c1)`

= `[c0*P³ + c2*P² + c3*P]/(P+c1)`. Let me do polynomial division of `c0*P³/(P+c1)` = `c0*P² - c0*c1*P + c0*c1²  - c0*c1³/(P+c1)`. This gets complicated but the combined form is a rational function `P*(c0*P² + c2*P + c3)/(P+c1)`.

The GT can be written as: `P*[-0.01095*P² + (0.9198 + 0.9198)*P + 0.9198*...] / (7.531*P + 1)` — let me combine over common denominator `(7.531P+1)`:

GT = `[-0.01095*P²*(7.531P+1) + 0.9198*P*(7.531P+1) + 0.9198*P²] / (7.531P+1)`
= `P*[-0.08242P² - 0.01095P + 6.923P + 0.9198 + 0.9198P] / (7.531P+1)`
= `P*[-0.08242P² + 7.833P + 0.9198] / (7.531P+1)`

**Candidate 16** has form `P*(c0*P² + c2*P + c3)/(P + c1)`. Setting c1 = 1/7.531 ≈ 0.1328, and matching coefficients: c0 = -0.08242/7.531, c2 and c3 adjusted. Yes! This matches structurally.

The GT = `P*(-0.08242P² + 7.833P + 0.9198)/(7.531P + 1)` and candidate 16 = `P*(c0P² + c2P + c3)/(P + c1)`. These match with appropriate constants.
